font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">B</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-50">P_{B}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as <disp-formula id="deqn9" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm Max}(0,P_{\rm MIN}-P_{\rm AVG})\leq P_{B}\leq{D(1-M_{\rm MIN})^{2}\over 1-(1-M_{\rm MIN})^{2}}P_{F}.\eqno{\hbox{(9)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-51">{\rm Max}(0,P_{\rm MIN}-P_{\rm AVG})\leq P_{B}\leq{D(1-M_{\rm MIN})^{2}\over 1-(1-M_{\rm MIN})^{2}}P_{F}.\eqno{\hbox{(9)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{\rm Max}(0,P_{\rm MIN}-P_{\rm AVG})\leq P_{B}\leq{D(1-M_{\rm MIN})^{2}\over 1-(1-M_{\rm MIN})^{2}}P_{F}.\eqno{\hbox{(9)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p><p>As in the proof shown in the <a ref-type="app" anchor="app1" class="fulltext-link">Appendix</a>, the optimum <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{B}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-52-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-52">P_{B}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> that results in the longest read range of the EPT is <disp-formula id="deqn10" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{B}={(1-\beta)Dk\over(1-\beta)Dk+1-x}P_{\rm MIN} \eqno{\hbox{(10)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-53-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-53">P_{B}={(1-\beta)Dk\over(1-\beta)Dk+1-x}P_{\rm MIN} \eqno{\hbox{(10)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">P_{B}={(1-\beta)Dk\over(1-\beta)Dk+1-x}P_{\rm MIN} \eqno{\hbox{(10)}}</span></span></disp-formula>where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">k=(1-M_{\rm MIN})^{2}/(1-(1-M_{\rm MIN})^{2})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-54-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-54">k=(1-M_{\rm MIN})^{2}/(1-(1-M_{\rm MIN})^{2})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta=xP_{R}/P_{\rm AVG}=T_{R}P_{R}/(T_{F}P_{F}+T_{R}P_{R})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-55">\beta=xP_{R}/P_{\rm AVG}=T_{R}P_{R}/(T_{F}P_{F}+T_{R}P_{R})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. It is noteworthy that <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-56">\beta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is a ratio that indicates the distribution of reader transmission power. Given a fixed reader transmission power, to lower the value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-57">\beta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is to lower the reader transmission power during the period <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">T_{R}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-58-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-58">T_{R}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, where only an unmodulated CW is sent by the reader. In other words, by reducing the value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-59-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-59">\beta</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, more power is transmitted in a reader command, which can alleviate the constraint of modulation depth of a received reader command that limits the tag read range, as stated in the <a ref-type="app" anchor="app1" class="fulltext-link">Appendix</a>.</p><p>By using optimum <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{B}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-60-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-60">P_{B}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the maximum read range of the EPT can be obtained as <disp-formula id="deqn11" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d_{{\rm MAX},{\rm EPT}}=\sqrt{\left((1-\beta)Dk+1-x\right)\alpha P_{\rm EIRP}\over(1-x)P_{\rm MIN}}.\eqno{\hbox{(11)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-61">d_{{\rm MAX},{\rm EPT}}=\sqrt{\left((1-\beta)Dk+1-x\right)\alpha P_{\rm EIRP}\over(1-x)P_{\rm MIN}}.\eqno{\hbox{(11)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">d_{{\rm MAX},{\rm EPT}}=\sqrt{\left((1-\beta)Dk+1-x\right)\alpha P_{\rm EIRP}\over(1-x)P_{\rm MIN}}.\eqno{\hbox{(11)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p><p>Equation <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn11" href="#deqn11" class="fulltext-link">(11)</a> represents that <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d_{\rm MAX}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-62-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-62">d_{\rm MAX}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> increases as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-63-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-63">\beta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> decreases.</p><p>Considering the path loss only, the maximum read range of a C1G2 tag in the forward link can be written as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d_{{\rm MAX},C1G2}=\sqrt{\alpha P_{\rm EIRP}/P_{\rm MIN}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-64-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-64">d_{{\rm MAX},C1G2}=\sqrt{\alpha P_{\rm EIRP}/P_{\rm MIN}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Comparing the two maximum read ranges, we can express the ratio of read range extension as <disp-formula id="deqn12" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{d_{{\rm MAX},{\rm EPT}}\over d_{{\rm MAX},C1G2}}=\sqrt{(1-\beta)Dk+1-x\over 1-x}.\eqno{\hbox{(12)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-65-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-65">{d_{{\rm MAX},{\rm EPT}}\over d_{{\rm MAX},C1G2}}=\sqrt{(1-\beta)Dk+1-x\over 1-x}.\eqno{\hbox{(12)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{d_{{\rm MAX},{\rm EPT}}\over d_{{\rm MAX},C1G2}}=\sqrt{(1-\beta)Dk+1-x\over 1-x}.\eqno{\hbox{(12)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p><p>Based on our measurement results of Texas Instrument (TI) Incorporated C1G2 tags, we have an approximation of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M_{\rm MIN}\cong 0.22</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-66-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-66">M_{\rm MIN}\cong 0.22</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Considering a regular Query command and 40-kHz FM0 encoding, we have <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">D\cong 1.47</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-67-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-67">D\cong 1.47</script></tex-math></inline-formula>; Using <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">T_{F}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-68-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-68">T_{F}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">T_{R}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-69-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-69">T_{R}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> indicated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a>, an approximate ratio <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">x\cong 0.62</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-70-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-70">x\cong 0.62</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is obtained. By substituting these parameters into <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn12" href="#deqn12" class="fulltext-link">(12)</a>, the maximum ratio of read range extension is about 2.65 for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta=0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-71-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-71">\beta=0</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. However, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta=0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-72-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-72">\beta=0</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is unrealistic because a reader needs to send an unmodulated CW as the carrier of the tag MBS. Similarly, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta=1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-73-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-73">\beta=1</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is also impractical since a reader has to send reader commands as well. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a> shows the optimum BAC power derived from <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn12" href="#deqn12" class="fulltext-link">(12)</a> with various values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M_{\rm MIN}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-74-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-74">M_{\rm MIN}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-75-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-75">\beta</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Likewise, the comparison of maximum EPT read-range extension with various <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M_{\rm MIN}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-76-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-76">M_{\rm MIN}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-77-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-77">\beta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a>.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Experimental Results</h2></div><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p>Optimum BAC power with various values of modulation depth limit <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M_{\rm MIN}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-78-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-78">M_{\rm MIN}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (which is denotes as M) and reader command power distribution ratio <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-79-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-79">\beta</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811951/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>Optimum EPT read range extension with various values of modulation depth limit <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M_{\rm MIN}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-80-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-80">M_{\rm MIN}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (which is denotes as M) and reader command power distribution ratio <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-81-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-81">\beta</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811951/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div> A prototype EPT is implemented by connecting a BAC to a regular TI C1G2 tag, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>.<p></p><p>Due to the size of the transition, the BAC is about two times larger than a TI C1G2 tag. We use a subminiature A (SMA) connector at the transition input so that the EPT source can be conveniently changed. An EPT source comprising a JTOS-850VW voltage-controlled oscillator (VCO),<a ref-type="fn" anchor="fn2" class="footnote-link"><sup>2</sup></a> peripheral circuit, and two batteries is also shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>.</p><p>In order to produce a suitable prototype EPT, further analysis is required. An equivalent circuit of the proposed EPT can be represented as <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a>, where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{T}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-82-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-82">Z_{T}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{A}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-83-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-83">Z_{A}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{B}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-84-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-84">Z_{B}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> denote the complex impedance of the tag IC, tag antenna, and added BAC. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{A}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-85-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-85">V_{A}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the votage induced in the antenna from received reader power, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{B}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-86-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-86">V_{B}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the source provided by a signal generator or an oscillator. Since <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{T}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-87-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-87">Z_{T}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is dependent to frequency and received power, it is very difficult to determine an optimal impedance of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{B}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-88-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-88">Z_{B}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In order not to interfere with the function of a regular tag, the impedance of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{B}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-89-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-89">Z_{B}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is desired to be as large as possible. However, if <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{B}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-90-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-90">Z_{B}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is too large, the power transfer from <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{B}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-91-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-91">V_{B}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to the tag IC will be reduced. Thus, to choose a good impedance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{B}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-92-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-92">Z_{B}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is not easy, especially with a variant tag IC impedance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{T}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-93-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-93">Z_{T}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Photograph of a prototype EPT.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811951/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 9. </b><fig><p>Equivalent circuit of the proposed EPT.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811951/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-10-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-10-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 10. </b><fig><p>Return loss of EPT.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811951/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div> The reflected signal generation power can be measured by the return loss from the SMA input of a prototype EPT, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10</a>. Due to the nonlinearity of the tag IC impedance <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_3">[12]</a>, the measured return loss also varies with different input power.<p></p><p>In addition, the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">S</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-94-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-94">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters of the transition using a back-to-back measurement are provided in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 11</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-11-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-11-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 11. </b><fig><p><inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">S</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-95-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-95">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters of the transition used in a prototype EPT.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811951/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Since the attached BAC may draw some received reader power, the reader signal leakage is measured as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 12</a>. The measurement is done by sending 915-MHz unmodulated CWs with various power levels toward an EPT and a spectrum analyzer is used to measure the output power from the SMA connector of the EPT. The loss of each transition calculated using the measured <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">S</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-96-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-96">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters has been considered and compensated in the measurement. It is noteworthy that without an IC, the ratio of the power flowing into the BAC to the incident power is almost fixed as 26.6%. However, the power leakage in a prototype EPT with an IC behaves nonlinearly when the tag IC is activated (incident power greater than −8 dBm). Note that the tag IC can be activated at −9 dBm according to <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_3">[12]</a>. Apparently, when the tag IC is activated, only a small portion of the reader signal flows into the BAC. Thus, the transition works as a power-dependent filter that can reduce the power leakage when the tag is activated.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig12"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-12-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-12-small.gif" alt="Figure 12" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 12. </b><fig><p>Reader power leakage into the transition.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811951/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Considering the intentional interference cause by the BAC, the radiation power at various directions of the EPT main beam are measured with an 800-MHz–11.94-dBm input power (the largest power we used in this study) is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 13</a>, which indicates the actual radiation powers are in the order of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu{\hbox{W}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-97-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-97">\mu{\hbox{W}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. If an antenna with a lower gain in the BAC operating frequency and high gain in the RFID operating band is used, the intentional radiation power can be further reduced without the tag performance degradation.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig13"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-13-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-13-small.gif" alt="Figure 13" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 13. </b><fig><p>Radiation power at various directions of the EPT main beam are measured with an 800-MHz–11.94-dBm input power. The radiation powers in three IC statuses are slightly different.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811951/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Due to the attached BAC, the EPT antenna power pattern slightly changes, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14</a>. Although the variation of antenna gains could affect the read range comparison of a zero-powered EPT and a regular C1G2 tag, it does not affect the read range comparison of a powerless EPT and a powered EPT because the same EPT is used.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig14"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-14-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-14-small.gif" alt="Figure 14" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 14. </b><fig><p>Antenna power pattern comparison of a prototype EPT and a regular tag.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811951/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Since the link budget in the forward link determines the read range of a present C1G2 tag, we measure the maximum distance where the tag can correctly respond to a reader command in our experiments. The reverse link signal strength measurement is, hence, not in the scope of this study. A schematic of our experiment setup is illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 15</a>. The transmitter in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 15</a> is emulated by an Agilent E4438C vector signal generator with a horn antenna, which sends a Query command toward the test tag. The receiver antenna in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 15</a> is connected to an Agilent 89611A vector signal analyzer, which can monitor and record signals from the transmitter and the tag. By using Agilent RFID modulation analysis software, the tag response can also be decoded. To measure the maximum read range of an EPT without multipath fading, we perform the test in the National Taiwan University of Science and Technology (NTUST) microwave anechoic chamber. In order to obtain a more accurate result, a horn antenna as the receiver antenna is used behind the transmitter antenna, i.e., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{3}&gt;R_{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-98-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-98">R_{3}&gt;R_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. On the other hand, to verify the performance of an EPT with multipath fading, the EPT is tested at a 230-cm-wide and 270-cm-high concrete hallway in the International Building of NTUST. In the measurement at the hallway, a standard dipole antenna is used as the receiver antenna, which is located 33 cm <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(R_{2}=33\ {\hbox{cm}})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-99-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-99">(R_{2}=33\ {\hbox{cm}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> away from the tested tag.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig15"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-15-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-15-small.gif" alt="Figure 15" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 15. </b><fig><p>Schematic of the experiment setup; SG denotes a signal generator, which can also be used as the EPT power source. A dipole antenna is used in the measurement in the hallway and the distance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{2}=33\ {\hbox{cm}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-100-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-100">R_{2}=33\ {\hbox{cm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Inside a chamber, in order to obtain a more accurate result, a horn antenna as the receiver antenna is used behind the transmitter antenna, i.e., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{3}&gt;R_{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-101-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-101">R_{3}&gt;R_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811951/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. Experiment Results in the Chamber</h3><p>Inside the chamber, we let the transmitter iteratively send Query commands to the test tag with 0.5-W EIRP, and use the receiver close to the tag to record the signals. A photograph of the experiment setup is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig16" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 16</a>. The measurements within 100 cm are skipped because there is no access problem. Snapshots of captured various reader commands and the corresponding tag responses are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 17</a>–<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig18" class="fulltext-link"></a>
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig19" class="fulltext-link">19</a>, respectively. Note that, the “x” in the above figures indicates an FM0 violation (i.e., a phase inversion should have occurred, but did not) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_3a">[4]</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig16"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-16-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-16-small.gif" alt="Figure 16" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 16. </b><fig><p>Photograph of the experiment inside the NTUST microwave anechoic chamber.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811951/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig17"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-17-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-17-small.gif" alt="Figure 17" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 17. </b><fig><p>Top window shows regular Query commands <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(\beta\cong 0.54)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-102-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-102">(\beta\cong 0.54)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the corresponding EPT responses. The middle window illustrates the MBS clearly. The decoded MBS (shadowed) comprising the preamble and the RN16 are depicted in the bottom window.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811951/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig18"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-18-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-18-small.gif" alt="Figure 18" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 18. </b><fig><p>Top window shows modified Query commands <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(\beta\cong0.43)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-103-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-103">(\beta\cong0.43)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the corresponding EPT responses. The middle window illustrates the MBS clearly. The decoded MBS (shadowed) comprising the preamble and the RN16 are depicted in the bottom window.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811951/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig19"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-19-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-19-small.gif" alt="Figure 19" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 19. </b><fig><p>Top window shows modified Query commands <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(\beta\cong 0.3)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-104-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-104">(\beta\cong 0.3)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the corresponding EPT responses. The middle window illustrates the MBS clearly. The decoded MBS (shadowed) comprising the preamble and the RN16 are depicted in the bottom window.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811951/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>In <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 17</a>, an 800-MHz–11.17-dBm unmodulated CW is generated from the BAC, and regular Generation-2 Query commands <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(\beta\cong 0.54)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-105-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-105">(\beta\cong 0.54)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are sent from the transmitter. The snapshot clearly shows that an EPT replies each reader command with the preambles and the RN16 (16 random bits) using a 40-kHz FM0 encoding MBS. The MBS is decoded by the Agilent RFID modulation analysis software, as illustrated in the bottom window. Note that the −11.17 dBm is the power of the unmodulated CW generated by the VCO. The actual transferred power into the tag IC could be lower.</p><p>In <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig18" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 18</a>, an 800-MHz–10.9-dBm unmodulated CW from the BAC is used, and modified Query commands with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta\cong 0.43</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-106-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-106">\beta\cong 0.43</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are sent from the transmitter. Similarly, in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig19" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 19</a>, an 800-MHz–10.45-dBm unmodulated CW from the BAC is used, and modified Query commands with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta\cong 0.3</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-107-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-107">\beta\cong 0.3</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are sent from the transmitter. As shown in both snapshots, an EPT can successfully decode the reader commands and reply its MBS accordingly.</p><p>Comparing <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 17</a>–<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig18" class="fulltext-link"></a>
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig19" class="fulltext-link">19</a>, the differences of Query commands with different <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-108-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-108">\beta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> values can be told easily. As shown in these figures, the lower the value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-109-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-109">\beta</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the stronger the power of a Query command.</p><p>The maximum read range comparison of an EPT and a regular C1G2 tag is presented in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig20" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 20</a>. For a regular reader command <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(\beta\cong 0.54)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-110-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-110">(\beta\cong 0.54)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the EPT <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(P_{B}=-13.64\ {\hbox{dBm}})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-111-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-111">(P_{B}=-13.64\ {\hbox{dBm}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> demonstrates a remarkable read range extension compared with a regular C1G2 tag. The maximum read ranges of the EPT with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta=0.43</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-112-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-112">\beta=0.43</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{B}=-12.74\ {\hbox{dBm}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-113-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-113">P_{B}=-12.74\ {\hbox{dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta=0.3</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-114-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-114">\beta=0.3</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{B}=-12.04\ {\hbox{dBm}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-115-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-115">P_{B}=-12.04\ {\hbox{dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are even longer. It is noteworthy that a powerless EPT can still function as a regular C1G2 tag, as depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig20" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 20</a> with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta=0.54</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-116-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-116">\beta=0.54</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{B}=0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-117-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-117">P_{B}=0</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The read range of the EPT without input power is almost the same as a regular C1G2 tag. However, due to the different antenna gains, it is difficult to compare the performance of a C1G2 tag and an EPT in terms of read range.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig20"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-20-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-20-small.gif" alt="Figure 20" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 20. </b><fig><p>Read range comparison inside the NTUST microwave anechoic chamber, where the first bar denotes the read range of a regular C1G2 tag, and the second bar (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta=0.54</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-118-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-118">\beta=0.54</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{B}=0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-119-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-119">P_{B}=0</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) denotes the read range of a powerless EPT.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811951/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig21"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-21-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-21-small.gif" alt="Figure 21" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 21. </b><fig><p>Photograph of the experiment at a hallway of the International Building, NTUST.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811951/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3b"><h3>B. Experiment Results at the Hallway</h3><p>Similar to the chamber experiments, the transmitter iteratively sends Query commands to the tag using 1-W EIRP. Since there are copious propagation paths at the concrete hallway, the severe multipath fading results in unstable readability and a shorter read range of a C1G2 tag. A photograph of our measurement is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig21" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 21</a>. Likewise, the measurements within 100 cm are skipped because there is no access problem. The tags are measured every 5 cm thereafter. A read range comparison result of an experiment is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig22" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 22</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig22"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-22-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811951/4811951-fig-22-small.gif" alt="Figure 22" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 22. </b><fig><p>Read range comparison at a hallway of the International Building, NTUST, where the first bar denotes the read range of a regular C1G2 tag, and the second bar (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta=0.54</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-120-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-120">\beta=0.54</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{B}=0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-121-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-121">P_{B}=0</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) denotes the read range of a powerless EPT.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811951/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>As shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig22" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 22</a>, the tested regular C1G2 tag can be read stably within 255 cm. Due to the multipath fading, the C1G2 tag can be read in some regions after 290 cm. The C1G2 tag cannot be read after 400 cm due to its power requirement constraint. Under the same condition, the tested EPT with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{B}=-13.65\ {\hbox{dBm}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-122-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-122">P_{B}=-13.65\ {\hbox{dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be read stably within 435 cm with two short gaps, where the multipath fading are severe as indicated in the bottom widow of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig22" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 22</a>. The EPT cannot be read after 460 cm using a regular Query command <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(\beta=0.54)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-123-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-123">(\beta=0.54)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> due to the reader command modulation depth constraint. Utilizing modified Query commands (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta=0.43</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-124-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-124">\beta=0.43</script></tex-math></inline-formula> or <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\beta=0.3</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-125-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-125">\beta=0.3</script></tex-math></inline-formula>), the longest read range of the EPT can be extended to 650 cm or so, despite that there is a 1-m gap due to a deep multipath fading. It is also noteworthy that the multipath fading before 470 cm does not affect the readability of the EPT with battery power.</p><p>As illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig22" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 22</a>, the EPT with battery power shows an excellent overall performance improvement in terms of the maximum read range and fading resistant capability.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Conclusions</h2></div><p>The prototype EPT demonstrates significant performance improvement in terms of read range extension and fading resistant capability. Due to utilizing a regular C1G2 tag IC, an EPT behaves as a regular C1G2 tag. When a modified reader command (by changing the power distribution of a reader command without reader average power increment) is used, the performance of an EPT can be further improved. However, the power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{R}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-126-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-126">P_{R}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> cannot be too low; otherwise, the reverse-link-limited range can be shorter than the forward-link-limited range. Moreover, a very low <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{R}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-127-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-127">P_{R}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can also result in a tag power outage when it backscatters its MBS. It is noteworthy that an EPT can be continuously used as a regular C1G2 tag after it uses up its battery power.</p><p>Compared with a regular C1G2 tag in the same access range, an EPT requires less reader power. This advantage can be very attractive in the applications using low-power mobile readers.</p><p>The prototype EPT still needs some improvements. First, as seen in the prototype EPT, the transition with an SMA connector is convenient for many experiments; however, the transition and other components are too big and costly compared with a C1G2 tag. Using a CMOS VCO IC and an antenna integrated with a battery is necessary for producing a commercialized EPT. Second, finding the optimal impedances of the BAC and antenna for an EPT is a complicated problem due to the nonlinearity of the IC impedance, which requires further investigation. Third, the size, cost, and life span of a battery are very challenging factors in practical EPT usages. Since the power requirement of an EPT is very low (in the order of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu{\hbox{W}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-128-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-128">\mu{\hbox{W}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>), utilizing the technology of rechargeable paper battery could be a good solution for this problem.</p></div>

Ma, both with National Taiwan University of Science and Technology, Taipei, Taiwan, for their valuable comments on this work. The authors also appreciate the valuable help from P.-C. Chen, D.-C. Hsin, and W.-C. Lin, all with National Taiwan University of Science and Technology, for their assistance with measurements and simulations.</p>
<div class="section" id="app1"><h2></h2><p>In order to derive the optimum value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{B}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-129-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-129">P_{B}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, we use <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn2" href="#deqn2" class="fulltext-link">(2)</a> to substitute <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{F}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-130-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-130">P_{F}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn9" href="#deqn9" class="fulltext-link">(9)</a> and rewrite <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn9" href="#deqn9" class="fulltext-link">(9)</a> as <disp-formula id="deqnA1" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Max(0,P_{\rm MIN}-P_{\rm AVG})\leq P_{B}\leq Dk\left({P_{\rm AVG}-xP_{R}\over 1-x}\right) \eqno{\hbox{(A1)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-131-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-131">Max(0,P_{\rm MIN}-P_{\rm AVG})\leq P_{B}\leq Dk\left({P_{\rm AVG}-xP_{R}\over 1-x}\right) \eqno{\hbox{(A1)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">Max(0,P_{\rm MIN}-P_{\rm AVG})\leq P_{B}\leq Dk\left({P_{\rm AVG}-xP_{R}\over 1-x}\right) \eqno{\hbox{(A1)}}</span></span></disp-formula>where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">k=(1-M_{\rm MIN})^{2}/(1-(1-M_{\rm MIN})^{2})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-132-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-132">k=(1-M_{\rm MIN})^{2}/(1-(1-M_{\rm MIN})^{2})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>Assuming that the tag is far away from the reader and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm AVG}&lt;P_{\rm MIN}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-133-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-133">P_{\rm AVG}&lt;P_{\rm MIN}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, we can individually examine the inequalities in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqnA1" href="#deqnA1" class="fulltext-link">(A1)</a>, and have <disp-formula id="deqnA2" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm AVG}\geq P_{\rm MIN}-P_{B} \eqno{\hbox{(A2)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-134-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-134">P_{\rm AVG}\geq P_{\rm MIN}-P_{B} \eqno{\hbox{(A2)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">P_{\rm AVG}\geq P_{\rm MIN}-P_{B} \eqno{\hbox{(A2)}}</span></span></disp-formula>and <disp-formula id="deqnA3" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm AVG}\geq{1-x\over Dk}P_{B}+xP_{R}.\eqno{\hbox{(A3)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-135-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-135">P_{\rm AVG}\geq{1-x\over Dk}P_{B}+xP_{R}.\eqno{\hbox{(A3)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">P_{\rm AVG}\geq{1-x\over Dk}P_{B}+xP_{R}.\eqno{\hbox{(A3)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p><p>When considering a free-space path loss only, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm AVG}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-136-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-136">P_{\rm AVG}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is reverse proportional to the square of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-137-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-137">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-138-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-138">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the distance between the tag and reader. Apparently, <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqnA2" href="#deqnA2" class="fulltext-link">(A2)</a> represents the tag minimum power constraint that limits the read range of an EPT. On the other hand, <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqnA3" href="#deqnA3" class="fulltext-link">(A3)</a> represents the constraint of modulation depth of a received reader command, which also limits the read range of the EPT.</p><p>Let <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm AVG}=\alpha P_{\rm EIRP}/d^{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-139-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-139">P_{\rm AVG}=\alpha P_{\rm EIRP}/d^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\alpha</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-140-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-140">\alpha</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is a constant taking the factors of reader signal wavelength and tag antenna gain into account, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm EIRP}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-141-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-141">P_{\rm EIRP}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> denotes the EIRP of the reader signal. The distance square <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d^{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-142-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-142">d^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be derived from <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqnA2" href="#deqnA2" class="fulltext-link">(A2)</a> as <disp-formula id="deqnA4" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d^{2}\leq{\alpha P_{\rm EIRP}\over P_{\rm MIN}-P_{B}}.\eqno{\hbox{(A4)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-143-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-143">d^{2}\leq{\alpha P_{\rm EIRP}\over P_{\rm MIN}-P_{B}}.\eqno{\hbox{(A4)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">d^{2}\leq{\alpha P_{\rm EIRP}\over P_{\rm MIN}-P_{B}}.\eqno{\hbox{(A4)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p><p>Let <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">xP_{R}=\beta P_{\rm AVG}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-144-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-144">xP_{R}=\beta P_{\rm AVG}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, we can rewrite <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqnA3" href="#deqnA3" class="fulltext-link">(A3)</a> as<disp-formula id="deqnA5" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d^{2}\leq{\alpha P_{\rm EIRP}\over{\displaystyle{1-x\over(1-\beta)Dk}}P_{B}}.\eqno{\hbox{(A5)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-145-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-145">d^{2}\leq{\alpha P_{\rm EIRP}\over{\displaystyle{1-x\over(1-\beta)Dk}}P_{B}}.\eqno{\hbox{(A5)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">d^{2}\leq{\alpha P_{\rm EIRP}\over{\displaystyle{1-x\over(1-\beta)Dk}}P_{B}}.\eqno{\hbox{(A5)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p><p>From <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqnA4" href="#deqnA4" class="fulltext-link">(A4)</a> and <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqnA5" href="#deqnA5" class="fulltext-link">(A5)</a>, the maximum read range <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-146-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-146">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in the forward link is obtained, when the denominators in both equations are equal, i.e., <disp-formula id="deqnA6" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm MIN}-P_{B}={1-x\over(1-\beta)Dk}P_{B}.\eqno{\hbox{(A6)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-147-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-147">P_{\rm MIN}-P_{B}={1-x\over(1-\beta)Dk}P_{B}.\eqno{\hbox{(A6)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">P_{\rm MIN}-P_{B}={1-x\over(1-\beta)Dk}P_{B}.\eqno{\hbox{(A6)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p><p>The optimum <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{B}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-148-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-148">P_{B}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> that results in the longest read range of the EPT can be derived from <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqnA6" href="#deqnA6" class="fulltext-link">(A6)</a> as <disp-formula id="deqnA7" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{B}={(1-\beta)Dk\over(1-\beta)Dk+1-x}P_{\rm MIN}.\eqno{\hbox{(A7)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-149-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-149">P_{B}={(1-\beta)Dk\over(1-\beta)Dk+1-x}P_{\rm MIN}.\eqno{\hbox{(A7)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">P_{B}={(1-\beta)Dk\over(1-\beta)Dk+1-x}P_{\rm MIN}.\eqno{\hbox{(A7)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p><p>By substituting <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqnA7" href="#deqnA7" class="fulltext-link">(A7)</a> into either <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqnA4" href="#deqnA4" class="fulltext-link">(A4)</a> or <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqnA5" href="#deqnA5" class="fulltext-link">(A5)</a>, the maximum read range of the EPT can be derived as <disp-formula id="deqnA8" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d_{{\rm MAX},{\rm EPT}}=\sqrt{\left((1-\beta)Dk+1-x\right)\alpha P_{\rm EIRP}\over(1-x)P_{\rm MIN}}.\eqno{\hbox{(A8)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-150-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-150">d_{{\rm MAX},{\rm EPT}}=\sqrt{\left((1-\beta)Dk+1-x\right)\alpha P_{\rm EIRP}\over(1-x)P_{\rm MIN}}.\eqno{\hbox{(A8)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">d_{{\rm MAX},{\rm EPT}}=\sqrt{\left((1-\beta)Dk+1-x\right)\alpha P_{\rm EIRP}\over(1-x)P_{\rm MIN}}.\eqno{\hbox{(A8)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>

The BAC generates a low-power unmodulated continuous wave with frequency outside the tag operating band to supply additional power to the tag. Empirical results demonstrate that a prototype EPT has a much longer read range and is more resistant to multipath fading than a regular class-1 generation-2 tag. Unlike a semipassive tag that depends on its local battery to work, a powerless EPT can function as a regular class-1 generation-2 tag.
